I want to create a capstone project and below are the details. 
This is an ambitious and highly relevant capstone project. By combining geographic data filtering with sophisticated AI architectures like RAG and Agentic workflows, you are moving beyond a simple search tool into a "Decision Engine."
Here is a structured proposal for your capstone project:
1. Project Title
EduNavigator AI: An Agentic RAG Framework for Hyper-Local Academic Mapping
* Alternative Title: Pathfinder AI: Precision Educational Discovery via Decentralized Agents
2. Project Description
EduNavigator AI is a comprehensive educational intelligence platform designed to simplify the complex process of school and university selection. Unlike static directories, this project utilizes Agentic AI to dynamically navigate through vast datasets—from local preschools to specialized graduate programs.
"The system employs a multi-layered Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) architecture to pull real-time, high-fidelity data regarding school ratings, tuition fees, and application requirements. Beyond basic data retrieval, the engine incorporates Agentic AI to provide strategic Advanced Placement (AP) and higher-level class selection suggestions, curated resources for college success, and deep insights into college life. This includes autonomous scouting for scholarships, as well as the discovery of clubs and organizations, ensuring a 360-degree view of the student’s potential academic and social journey.". By using a multi-agent system, the application can "act" on behalf of the user: one agent might handle geographic filtering, another performs deep-web scraping for the latest fee structures, and a third synthesizes personalized application checklists.
3. Project Problem Statement
Prospective students and parents currently face "Information Overload" and "Data Fragmentation" when searching for educational institutions.
* The Fragmentation Gap: Reliable data on K-12 schools, charter options, and higher education is often stored in disparate government databases, private review sites, and individual institutional portals.
* The Static Data Issue: Traditional search engines often provide outdated fee structures or broken application links.
* The Lack of Personalization: Existing tools rarely offer a "one-stop" journey from broad geographic discovery to granular, document-level application guidance.
4. Proposed Solutions
To solve these challenges, the project will implement the following technical solutions:
A. Hierarchical Geographic Filtering (Multi-Stage UI)
A Streamlit-based interface that implements a cascading selection logic (State $\rightarrow$ County $\rightarrow$ Education Level). This ensures the "Search Space" is optimized before the AI begins its retrieval process.
B. Agentic RAG Framework
Instead of a simple database query, the system will use AI Agents to:
* The Librarian Agent (RAG): Accesses a vector database of school profiles to provide the "2-3 line" summaries and basic info.
* The Researcher Agent (Agentic Web Search): If the database info is incomplete, this agent uses tools (like Tavily or Google Search) to find real-time ratings and current "How to Apply" instructions.
* The Document Specialist Agent: Analyzes specific admission requirements to generate a customized PDF checklist for the user.
C. Advanced Prompt Engineering
The project will utilize Chain-of-Thought (CoT) prompting to ensure the AI accurately compares schools based on complex metrics like ROI (Return on Investment) for colleges or teacher-to-student ratios for preschools.You are my project manager and mentor. But i have installed python 3.14. is that ok? or do i need to install python 3.11?Mar 28Great question! Python 3.14 is very new (still in pre-release/beta as of early 2026), which actually causes problems for this project. Here's the situation:

The Problem with Python 3.14 for This Project
Several libraries in our stack — especially chromadb, sentence-transformers, and langchain — have not yet released stable builds for Python 3.14. This means you'll likely hit errors like:
ERROR: Could not find a version that satisfies the requirement chromadb==0.5.3
or
error: Microsoft Visual C++ 14.0 or greater is required
These are notoriously painful to debug on Windows.

Recommendation — Keep Both, Use 3.11 for This Project
You don't need to uninstall 3.14. Python lets you have multiple versions side by side. Here's what to do:
Step 1 — Download Python 3.11
Go to: https://www.python.org/downloads/release/python-3119/
Scroll down to "Files" → download "Windows installer (64-bit)"
During installation:

✅ Check "Add Python 3.11 to PATH"
✅ Check "Install for all users"

Step 2 — Verify both versions exist
Open a new terminal and run:
bashpy -3.11 --version
py -3.14 --version
Both should respond with their version numbers.
Step 3 — Recreate the virtual environment using 3.11
If you already created the venv folder from Phase 1, delete it first:
bashcd EduNavigatorAI
rmdir /s /q venv
Then recreate it specifically with 3.11:
bashpy -3.11 -m venv venv
venv\Scripts\activate
Confirm it's using 3.11:
bashpython --version
You should see Python 3.11.x — and now all library installs from Phase 1 will work perfectly.

Quick Summary
Python 3.14Python 3.11StatusBeta / pre-releaseStable, fully supportedChromaDB support❌ Broken✅ Workssentence-transformers❌ May fail✅ WorksLangChain❌ Unstable✅ WorksKeep installed?✅ Yes, for other use✅ Yes, use for this project

Once you've done this, run python --version inside your activated venv and confirm it shows 3.11.x, then proceed with pip install -r requirements.txt from Phase 1. That error code 0x80073cf1 is a Windows Store package error and it's a known Windows bug. Just ignore it completely. We'll work around it by simply installing 3.11 alongside 3.14.

The Fix — Install 3.11 Without Touching 3.14
Step 1 — Download Python 3.11 Installer
Go to this exact link:
👉 https://www.python.org/downloads/release/python-3119/
Scroll to the bottom to the Files table and click:
"Windows installer (64-bit)"
Step 2 — Install it carefully

Click Install


Step 3 — Verify Both Pythons Exist
Open a brand new terminal in VS Code (Ctrl + ~) and run:
bashpy -3.11 --version
bashpy -3.14 --version
Expected output:
Python 3.11.9
Python 3.14.x
If both show up, you're in great shape.

Step 4 — Check py launcher is working
Run this to see all installed versions at once:
bashpy --list
Expected output:
 -V:3.14 *        Python 3.14
 -V:3.11          Python 3.11

Step 5 — Recreate the Virtual Environment with 3.11
Navigate to your project folder:
bashcd EduNavigatorAI
Delete the old venv if you made one:
bashrmdir /s /q venv
Create a fresh one using Python 3.11 specifically:
bashpy -3.11 -m venv venv

Confirm the version inside the venv:

You must see:
Python 3.11.9

Step 6 — Now install dependencies
bashpip install -r requirements.txt
This will now work cleanly because everything runs inside the 3.11 venv, and 3.14 is completely untouched and unaffected.

Why This Works
Think of the virtual environment like a sealed box. Once you create it with py -3.11, everything inside that box — Python, pip, all libraries — runs on 3.11 exclusively. Python 3.14 sits outside the box and never interferes.
Your Windows Machine
├── Python 3.14  ←  untouched, used for other things
├── Python 3.11  ←  installed fresh
└── EduNavigatorAI/
    └── venv/    ←  sealed box running 3.11 only ✅

Step 2 — Build the Embeddings Utility
Open utils/embeddings.py and paste this:
pythonimport os
import pandas as pd
import chromadb
from sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer
from dotenv import load_dotenv

load_dotenv()

CHROMA_DB_PATH = os.getenv("CHROMA_DB_PATH", "./chroma_db")
EMBED_MODEL = os.getenv("EMBED_MODEL", "all-MiniLM-L6-v2")
COLLECTION_NAME = "schools"


def build_school_documents(row):
    """
    Convert a CSV row into a rich text document for embedding.
    The richer the text, the better the RAG retrieval quality.
    """
    doc = f"""
    School Name: {row['name']}
    Type: {row['type']} | Level: {row['level']}
    Location: {row['city']}, {row['county']} County, {row['state']}
    Rating: {row['rating']}/10
    Tuition: ${row['tuition_min']} - ${row['tuition_max']} per year
    Students: {row['student_count']} | Teacher-Student Ratio: {row['teacher_student_ratio']}
    AP Courses Available: {row['ap_courses']}
    Clubs & Organizations: {row['clubs']} clubs
    Application Deadline: {row['application_deadline']}
    Website: {row['website']}
    Description: {row['description']}
    """.strip()
    return doc


def load_vector_db():
    """
    Load ChromaDB. If the collection already exists and has data,
    skip re-embedding to save time on subsequent runs.
    """
    client = chromadb.PersistentClient(path=CHROMA_DB_PATH)

    existing_collections = [c.name for c in client.list_collections()]
    if COLLECTION_NAME in existing_collections:
        collection = client.get_collection(COLLECTION_NAME)
        if collection.count() > 0:
            print(f"✅ ChromaDB already loaded with {collection.count()} schools. Skipping re-embedding.")
            return collection

    print("🔄 Building vector database from scratch...")
    collection = client.get_or_create_collection(
        name=COLLECTION_NAME,
        metadata={"hnsw:space": "cosine"}
    )

    df = pd.read_csv("data/schools.csv")
    model = SentenceTransformer(EMBED_MODEL)

    documents = []
    embeddings = []
    metadatas = []
    ids = []

    for _, row in df.iterrows():
        doc_text = build_school_documents(row)
        embedding = model.encode(doc_text).tolist()

        documents.append(doc_text)
        embeddings.append(embedding)
        ids.append(str(row["school_id"]))
        metadatas.append({
            "name":       str(row["name"]),
            "type":       str(row["type"]),
            "level":      str(row["level"]),
            "state":      str(row["state"]),
            "county":     str(row["county"]),
            "city":       str(row["city"]),
            "rating":     float(row["rating"]),
            "tuition_min":int(row["tuition_min"]),
            "tuition_max":int(row["tuition_max"]),
            "ap_courses": int(row["ap_courses"]),
            "clubs":      int(row["clubs"]),
            "website":    str(row["website"]),
        })

    collection.add(
        documents=documents,
        embeddings=embeddings,
        metadatas=metadatas,
        ids=ids
    )

    print(f"✅ Vector DB built successfully with {collection.count()} schools.")
    return collection


def query_vector_db(collection, query_text, filters=None, n_results=5):
    """
    Query ChromaDB with semantic search + optional metadata filters.
    filters example: {"state": "Texas", "level": "High School"}
    """
    model = SentenceTransformer(EMBED_MODEL)
    query_embedding = model.encode(query_text).tolist()

    where_clause = {}
    if filters:
        active = {k: v for k, v in filters.items() if v and v != "All"}
        if len(active) == 1:
            key, val = list(active.items())[0]
            where_clause = {key: val}
        elif len(active) > 1:
            where_clause = {"$and": [{k: v} for k, v in active.items()]}

    results = collection.query(
        query_embeddings=[query_embedding],
        n_results=n_results,
        where=where_clause if where_clause else None,
        include=["documents", "metadatas", "distances"]
    )

    return results

Step 3 — Build the Geographic Filter Utility
Open utils/geo_filter.py and paste this:
pythonimport pandas as pd


def load_geo_data(csv_path="data/schools.csv"):
    """Load and return the school dataframe."""
    return pd.read_csv(csv_path)


def get_states(df):
    """Return sorted list of unique states."""
    return sorted(df["state"].dropna().unique().tolist())


def get_counties(df, state):
    """Return sorted counties for a given state."""
    if not state or state == "All":
        return []
    filtered = df[df["state"] == state]
    return sorted(filtered["county"].dropna().unique().tolist())


def get_education_levels(df, state, county):
    """Return education levels available for state + county."""
    filtered = df.copy()
    if state and state != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["state"] == state]
    if county and county != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["county"] == county]
    return sorted(filtered["level"].dropna().unique().tolist())


def filter_schools(df, state=None, county=None, level=None):
    """
    Apply geographic + education level filters.
    Returns filtered dataframe.
    """
    filtered = df.copy()
    if state and state != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["state"] == state]
    if county and county != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["county"] == county]
    if level and level != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["level"] == level]
    return filtered.reset_index(drop=True)

# ── Test 3: Semantic Search ────────────────────────

queries = [
    ("best high school with AP courses in Texas", {"state": "Texas", "level": "High School"}),
    ("affordable university with engineering programs", {"state": "Texas", "level": "University"}),
    ("Montessori preschool with small class size", {"state": "Texas", "level": "Preschool"}),
]

for query_text, filters in queries:
    print(f"\n🔍 Query: '{query_text}'")
    print(f"   Filters: {filters}")
    results = query_vector_db(collection, query_text, filters=filters, n_results=3)
    for i, (doc, meta, dist) in enumerate(zip(
        results["documents"][0],
        results["metadatas"][0],
        results["distances"][0]
    )):
        score = round((1 - dist) * 100, 1)
        print(f"   #{i+1} {meta['name']} ({meta['city']}) — Match: {score}%")

Step 2 — Build the Geographic Filter Utility
Open utils/geo_filter.py and paste this:
pythonimport pandas as pd


def load_geo_data(csv_path="data/schools.csv"):
    """Load and return the school dataframe."""
    return pd.read_csv(csv_path)


def get_states(df):
    """Return sorted list of unique states."""
    return sorted(df["state"].dropna().unique().tolist())


def get_counties(df, state):
    """Return sorted counties for a given state."""
    if not state or state == "All":
        return []
    filtered = df[df["state"] == state]
    return sorted(filtered["county"].dropna().unique().tolist())


def get_education_levels(df, state, county):
    """Return education levels available for state + county."""
    filtered = df.copy()
    if state and state != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["state"] == state]
    if county and county != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["county"] == county]
    return sorted(filtered["level"].dropna().unique().tolist())


def filter_schools(df, state=None, county=None, level=None):
    """
    Apply geographic + education level filters.
    Returns filtered dataframe.
    """
    filtered = df.copy()
    if state and state != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["state"] == state]
    if county and county != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["county"] == county]
    if level and level != "All":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["level"] == level]
    return filtered.reset_index(drop=True)
Save the file (Ctrl + S).

Step 3 — Build the Embeddings Utility
Open utils/embeddings.py and paste this:
pythonimport os
import warnings
import pandas as pd
import chromadb
from sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer
from dotenv import load_dotenv

warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
load_dotenv()

CHROMA_DB_PATH = os.getenv("CHROMA_DB_PATH", "./chroma_db")
EMBED_MODEL    = os.getenv("EMBED_MODEL", "all-MiniLM-L6-v2")
COLLECTION     = "schools"


def build_document(row):
    """
    Convert one CSV row into a rich text document for embedding.
    The richer the text, the better the RAG retrieval quality.
    """
    return f"""
School Name: {row['name']}
Type: {row['type']} | Level: {row['level']}
Location: {row['city']}, {row['county']} County, {row['state']}
Rating: {row['rating']}/10
Tuition: ${row['tuition_min']} - ${row['tuition_max']} per year
Students: {row['student_count']} | Teacher-Student Ratio: {row['teacher_student_ratio']}
AP Courses Available: {row['ap_courses']}
Clubs and Organizations: {row['clubs']} clubs
Application Deadline: {row['application_deadline']}
Website: {row['website']}
Description: {row['description']}
""".strip()


def get_chroma_client():
    """Return a silent persistent ChromaDB client."""
    return chromadb.PersistentClient(path=CHROMA_DB_PATH)


def load_vector_db():
    """
    Load ChromaDB. If already populated, skip re-embedding
    to save time on subsequent runs.
    """
    client     = get_chroma_client()
    collection = client.get_or_create_collection(
        name=COLLECTION,
        metadata={"hnsw:space": "cosine"}
    )

    if collection.count() > 0:
        print(f"✅ ChromaDB already loaded with {collection.count()} schools.")
        return collection

    print("🔄 Building vector database — this takes ~30 seconds...")
    df    = pd.read_csv("data/schools.csv")
    model = SentenceTransformer(EMBED_MODEL)

    documents  = []
    embeddings = []
    metadatas  = []
    ids        = []

    for _, row in df.iterrows():
        text      = build_document(row)
        embedding = model.encode(text).tolist()

        documents.append(text)
        embeddings.append(embedding)
        ids.append(str(row["school_id"]))
        metadatas.append({
            "name":        str(row["name"]),
            "type":        str(row["type"]),
            "level":       str(row["level"]),
            "state":       str(row["state"]),
            "county":      str(row["county"]),
            "city":        str(row["city"]),
            "rating":      float(row["rating"]),
            "tuition_min": int(row["tuition_min"]),
            "tuition_max": int(row["tuition_max"]),
            "ap_courses":  int(row["ap_courses"]),
            "clubs":       int(row["clubs"]),
            "website":     str(row["website"]),
        })

    collection.add(
        documents=documents,
        embeddings=embeddings,
        metadatas=metadatas,
        ids=ids
    )

    print(f"✅ Vector DB built with {collection.count()} schools.")
    return collection


def query_vector_db(collection, query_text, filters=None, n_results=5):
    """
    Semantic search with optional metadata filters.
    filters example: {"state": "Texas", "level": "High School"}
    """
    model           = SentenceTransformer(EMBED_MODEL)
    query_embedding = model.encode(query_text).tolist()

    where_clause = {}
    if filters:
        active = {k: v for k, v in filters.items() if v and v != "All"}
        if len(active) == 1:
            key, val     = list(active.items())[0]
            where_clause = {key: val}
        elif len(active) > 1:
            where_clause = {"$and": [{k: v} for k, v in active.items()]}

    results = collection.query(
        query_embeddings=[query_embedding],
        n_results=n_results,
        where=where_clause if where_clause else None,
        include=["documents", "metadatas", "distances"]
    )

    return results
Save the file (Ctrl + S).

pythonimport warnings
warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")

from utils.embeddings import load_vector_db, query_vector_db
from utils.geo_filter import (
    load_geo_data, get_states,
    get_counties, get_education_levels,
    filter_schools
)

print("=" * 55)
print("   Phase 2 Test — Data Layer & Vector DB")
print("=" * 55)

# ── Test 1: Load Dataset ───────────────────────────
print("\n--- Test 1: Load Dataset ---")
df = load_geo_data()

# ── Test 2: Geographic Filter ──────────────────────

print(f"✅ Counties in Texas: {counties}")

queries = [
    (

        {"state": "Texas", "level": "High School"}
    ),

        "affordable university with engineering programs",
        {"state": "Texas", "level": "University"}
    ),
    (
        "Montessori preschool with small class sizes",
        {"state": "Texas", "level": "Preschool"}
    ),
]

for query_text, filters in queries:
    print(f"\n🔍 Query : '{query_text}'")
    print(f"   Filter: {filters}")

        collection, query_text,
        filters=filters, n_results=3
    )

        results["metadatas"][0],
        results["distances"][0]
    )):

Updated utils/geo_filter.py
Replace the entire content of utils/geo_filter.py with this:
pythonimport pandas as pd

# All US states for the dropdown
ALL_US_STATES = [
    "Alabama", "Alaska", "Arizona", "Arkansas", "California",
    "Colorado", "Connecticut", "Delaware", "Florida", "Georgia",
    "Hawaii", "Idaho", "Illinois", "Indiana", "Iowa",
    "Kansas", "Kentucky", "Louisiana", "Maine", "Maryland",
    "Massachusetts", "Michigan", "Minnesota", "Mississippi", "Missouri",
    "Montana", "Nebraska", "Nevada", "New Hampshire", "New Jersey",
    "New Mexico", "New York", "North Carolina", "North Dakota", "Ohio",
    "Oklahoma", "Oregon", "Pennsylvania", "Rhode Island", "South Carolina",
    "South Dakota", "Tennessee", "Texas", "Utah", "Vermont",
    "Virginia", "Washington", "West Virginia", "Wisconsin", "Wyoming"
]

# Education levels where county filter is NOT applicable
STATE_LEVEL_EDUCATION = [
    "University",
    "Community College"
]

# Education levels where county filter IS applicable
COUNTY_LEVEL_EDUCATION = [
    "High School",
    "Elementary",
    "Preschool",
    "Middle School"
]


def load_geo_data(csv_path="data/schools.csv"):
    """Load and return the school dataframe."""
    return pd.read_csv(csv_path)


def get_all_states():
    """Return full list of all US states."""
    return ALL_US_STATES


def get_education_levels():
    """
    Return all education levels in logical order.
    County filter will only activate for COUNTY_LEVEL_EDUCATION.
    """
    return [
        "Preschool",
        "Elementary",
        "Middle School",
        "High School",
        "Community College",
        "University"
    ]


def is_county_applicable(level):
    """
    Returns True if the selected education level
    requires a county filter, False otherwise.
    """
    return level in COUNTY_LEVEL_EDUCATION


def get_counties_for_level(df, state, level):
    """
    Return counties only if education level supports
    county-level filtering AND data exists for that state.
    Returns empty list for university/community college.
    """
    if not is_county_applicable(level):
        return []

    if not state or state == "Select State":
        return []

    filtered = df[
        (df["state"] == state) &
        (df["level"] == level)
    ]
    counties = sorted(filtered["county"].dropna().unique().tolist())
    return counties


def filter_schools(df, state=None, level=None, county=None):
    """
    Apply filters based on education level type.

    For University / Community College:
        filter by state + level only (ignore county)

    For High School and below:
        filter by state + level + county (if county selected)
    """
    filtered = df.copy()

    # Always filter by level first
    if level and level != "Select Level":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["level"] == level]

    # Always filter by state
    if state and state != "Select State":
        filtered = filtered[filtered["state"] == state]

    # Apply county only for lower education levels
    if is_county_applicable(level):
        if county and county != "Select County" and county != "All Counties":
            filtered = filtered[filtered["county"] == county]

    return filtered.reset_index(drop=True)


def get_filter_summary(state, level, county=None):
    """
    Returns a human-readable summary of active filters.
    Used to display context in the UI.
    """
    if not state or not level:
        return "Please select filters to begin."

    if is_county_applicable(level):
        if county and county not in ["Select County", "All Counties"]:
            return f"Showing {level} schools in {county} County, {state}"
        return f"Showing {level} schools in {state} (all counties)"
    else:
        return f"Showing {level} institutions in {state}"
Save the file (Ctrl + S).

Fix 1 — Increase Windows Virtual Memory (Paging File)
Step 1
Press Windows + R, type:
sysdm.cpl
Press Enter.
Step 2
Click "Advanced" tab → Under Performance click "Settings"
Step 3
Click "Advanced" tab → Under Virtual memory click "Change"
Step 4

✅ Uncheck "Automatically manage paging file size for all drives"
Select your C: drive
Select "Custom size"
Set these values:

Initial size: 4096
Maximum size: 8192

Click "Set" → Click "OK" → Click "OK" → Click "OK"

Step 5
Restart your computer — this step is mandatory, the change won't apply without a restart.

Fix 2 — Cache the Embedding Model (Prevents Reloading Every Query)
The current code reloads the embedding model on every single query which is very memory intensive. Let's fix that properly by loading it once and reusing it.
Open utils/embeddings.py and replace the entire file with this:
pythonimport os
import logging
import warnings
import pandas as pd
import chromadb
from chromadb.config import Settings
from sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer
from dotenv import load_dotenv

warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
logging.getLogger("chromadb").setLevel(logging.ERROR)
load_dotenv()

CHROMA_DB_PATH = os.getenv("CHROMA_DB_PATH", "./chroma_db")
EMBED_MODEL    = os.getenv("EMBED_MODEL", "all-MiniLM-L6-v2")
COLLECTION     = "schools"

# ── Load embedding model ONCE at module level ──────
# This prevents reloading on every query call
# and avoids the paging file memory error on Windows
print("🔄 Loading embedding model...")
_embed_model = SentenceTransformer(EMBED_MODEL)
print("✅ Embedding model loaded.")


def get_chroma_client():
    """Return a silent persistent ChromaDB client."""
    return chromadb.PersistentClient(
        path=CHROMA_DB_PATH,
        settings=Settings(
            anonymized_telemetry=False
        )
    )


def build_document(row):
    """
    Convert one CSV row into a rich text document for embedding.
    The richer the text, the better the RAG retrieval quality.
    """
    return f"""
School Name: {row['name']}
Type: {row['type']} | Level: {row['level']}
Location: {row['city']}, {row['county']} County, {row['state']}
Rating: {row['rating']}/10
Tuition: ${row['tuition_min']} - ${row['tuition_max']} per year
Students: {row['student_count']} | Teacher-Student Ratio: {row['teacher_student_ratio']}
AP Courses Available: {row['ap_courses']}
Clubs and Organizations: {row['clubs']} clubs
Application Deadline: {row['application_deadline']}
Website: {row['website']}
Description: {row['description']}
""".strip()


def load_vector_db():
    """
    Load ChromaDB. If already populated, skip re-embedding
    to save time on subsequent runs.
    """
    client     = get_chroma_client()
    collection = client.get_or_create_collection(
        name=COLLECTION,
        metadata={"hnsw:space": "cosine"}
    )

    if collection.count() > 0:
        print(f"✅ ChromaDB already loaded with {collection.count()} schools.")
        return collection

    print("🔄 Building vector database — this takes ~30 seconds...")
    df = pd.read_csv("data/schools.csv")

    documents  = []
    embeddings = []
    metadatas  = []
    ids        = []

    for _, row in df.iterrows():
        text      = build_document(row)
        embedding = _embed_model.encode(text).tolist()

        documents.append(text)
        embeddings.append(embedding)
        ids.append(str(row["school_id"]))
        metadatas.append({
            "name":        str(row["name"]),
            "type":        str(row["type"]),
            "level":       str(row["level"]),
            "state":       str(row["state"]),
            "county":      str(row["county"]),
            "city":        str(row["city"]),
            "rating":      float(row["rating"]),
            "tuition_min": int(row["tuition_min"]),
            "tuition_max": int(row["tuition_max"]),
            "ap_courses":  int(row["ap_courses"]),
            "clubs":       int(row["clubs"]),
            "website":     str(row["website"]),
        })

    collection.add(
        documents=documents,
        embeddings=embeddings,
        metadatas=metadatas,
        ids=ids
    )

    print(f"✅ Vector DB built with {collection.count()} schools.")
    return collection


def query_vector_db(collection, query_text, filters=None, n_results=5):
    """
    Semantic search with optional metadata filters.
    filters example: {"state": "Texas", "level": "High School"}
    """
    # Uses the cached model — no reloading
    query_embedding = _embed_model.encode(query_text).tolist()

    where_clause = {}
    if filters:
        active = {k: v for k, v in filters.items() if v and v != "All"}
        if len(active) == 1:
            key, val     = list(active.items())[0]
            where_clause = {key: val}
        elif len(active) > 1:
            where_clause = {"$and": [{k: v} for k, v in active.items()]}

    results = collection.query(
        query_embeddings=[query_embedding],
        n_results=n_results,
        where=where_clause if where_clause else None,
        include=["documents", "metadatas", "distances"]
    )

    return results
Save (Ctrl + S).

Final Telemetry Fix — Upgrade ChromaDB
The version we installed has a bug where it ignores the anonymized_telemetry=False setting. The fix is to upgrade it:
cmdpip install --upgrade chromadb
Then delete and rebuild:
cmdrmdir /s /q chroma_db
python test_phase2.py
You should now see completely clean output with zero telemetry lines.

If Telemetry Still Shows After Upgrade
Don't worry about it at all — it is 100% cosmetic. It does not affect your data, results, performance, or the final project in any way. We've tried every fix and this is a known unfixed bug in certain ChromaDB builds on Windows.

Then run again:
cmdpython test_phase2.py

Why This Happens
Every time you open a new terminal in VS Code, the virtual environment resets and needs to be reactivated manually. This is normal Windows behavior.
Golden rule — always run this first whenever you open a terminal:
cmdvenv\Scripts\activate
You'll know it's active when you see (venv) at the start of the line. If you don't see it, nothing will work because Python can't find any of the installed libraries.

pythonimport os
import warnings
import logging
warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
logging.getLogger("chromadb").setLevel(logging.ERROR)

import streamlit as st
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from utils.geo_filter import (
    load_geo_data,
    get_all_states,
    get_education_levels,
    is_county_applicable,
    get_counties_for_level,
    filter_schools,
    get_filter_summary
)
from utils.embeddings import load_vector_db, query_vector_db

load_dotenv()

# ── Page Configuration ─────────────────────────────
st.set_page_config(
    page_title="EduNavigator AI",
    page_icon="🎓",
    layout="wide",
    initial_sidebar_state="expanded"
)

# ── Custom CSS ─────────────────────────────────────

# ── Load Data & Vector DB ──────────────────────────
@st.cache_resource(show_spinner=False)
def get_resources():
    df         = load_geo_data()
    collection = load_vector_db()
    return df, collection


# ── Rating Helper ──────────────────────────────────
def get_rating_class(rating):
    if rating >= 9.0:
        return "rating-high"
    elif rating >= 8.0:
        return "rating-mid"
    return "rating-low"


def get_rating_emoji(rating):
    if rating >= 9.0:
        return "⭐ Excellent"
    elif rating >= 8.0:
        return "👍 Good"
    return "📌 Average"


# ── School Card Renderer ───────────────────────────
def render_school_card(row):
    rating       = float(row["rating"])
    rating_class = get_rating_class(rating)
    rating_label = get_rating_emoji(rating)

    # Tuition display
    if int(row["tuition_min"]) == 0 and int(row["tuition_max"]) == 0:
        tuition_text = "Free (Public)"
    else:
        tuition_text = f"${int(row['tuition_min']):,} – ${int(row['tuition_max']):,}/yr"

    # AP courses chip (only for high school)
    ap_chip = ""
    if int(row["ap_courses"]) > 0:
        ap_chip = f'<span class="chip">📚 {row["ap_courses"]} AP Courses</span>'

    st.markdown(f"""
    <div class="school-card">
        <div class="school-name">🏫 {row['name']}</div>
        <div class="school-meta">
            📍 {row['city']}, {row['county']} County, {row['state']} &nbsp;|&nbsp;
            🏷️ {row['type']} {row['level']}
        </div>
        <div class="school-description">{row['description']}</div>
        <span class="rating-badge {rating_class}">
            {rating_label} &nbsp; {rating}/10
        </span> &nbsp;
        <span class="chip">💰 {tuition_text}</span>
        <span class="chip">👥 {int(row['student_count']):,} students</span>
        <span class="chip">👩‍🏫 Ratio {row['teacher_student_ratio']}</span>
        <span class="chip">🎭 {row['clubs']} clubs</span>
        {ap_chip}
        <br><br>
        <span style="font-size:0.8rem; color:#888;">
            🗓️ Deadline: {row['application_deadline']} &nbsp;|&nbsp;
            🌐 {row['website']}
        </span>
    </div>
    """, unsafe_allow_html=True)


# ── Main App ───────────────────────────────────────
def main():
    # Header
    st.markdown("""
    <div class="main-header">
        <h1>🎓 EduNavigator AI</h1>
        <p>Intelligent School & University Discovery Platform</p>
    </div>
    """, unsafe_allow_html=True)

    # Load resources
    with st.spinner("Loading EduNavigator AI..."):
        df, collection = get_resources()

    # ── Sidebar Filters ────────────────────────────
    with st.sidebar:
        st.markdown('<div class="sidebar-title">🔍 Search Filters</div>',
                    unsafe_allow_html=True)

        # Step 1: Education Level (always first)
        st.markdown("**Step 1 — Select Education Level**")
        level_options = ["Select Level"] + get_education_levels()
        selected_level = st.selectbox(
            "Education Level",
            options=level_options,
            key="level",
            label_visibility="collapsed"
        )

        # Step 2: State
        st.markdown("**Step 2 — Select State**")
        state_options  = ["Select State"] + get_all_states()
        selected_state = st.selectbox(
            "State",
            options=state_options,
            key="state",
            label_visibility="collapsed"
        )

        # Step 3: County (only for lower education levels)
        selected_county = None
        county_active   = (
            selected_level not in ["Select Level"] and
            is_county_applicable(selected_level)
        )

        if county_active:
            st.markdown("**Step 3 — Select County**")
            counties = get_counties_for_level(
                df, selected_state, selected_level
            )
            if counties:
                county_options  = ["All Counties"] + counties
                selected_county = st.selectbox(
                    "County",
                    options=county_options,
                    key="county",
                    label_visibility="collapsed"
                )
            else:
                if selected_state != "Select State":
                    st.info(
                        f"No {selected_level} data found "
                        f"in {selected_state} yet."
                    )
                selected_county = None
        else:
            if selected_level not in ["Select Level"]:
                st.markdown("**Step 3 — County**")
                st.info(
                    f"County filter is not applicable "
                    f"for {selected_level} level."
                )

        st.divider()

        # Search query box
        st.markdown("**💬 What are you looking for?**")
        search_query = st.text_area(
            "Search query",
            placeholder=(
                "e.g. best school with strong STEM program\n"
                "e.g. affordable university with scholarships\n"
                "e.g. Montessori with small class sizes"
            ),
            height=100,
            label_visibility="collapsed"
        )

        # Number of results
        st.markdown("**📊 Number of Results**")
        n_results = st.slider(
            "Results", min_value=1,
            max_value=10, value=5,
            label_visibility="collapsed"
        )

        st.divider()

        # Search button
        search_clicked = st.button(
            "🔍 Search Schools",
            use_container_width=True,
            type="primary"
        )

    # ── Main Content Area ──────────────────────────
    filters_ready = (
        selected_level != "Select Level" and
        selected_state != "Select State"
    )

    if not filters_ready:
        # Welcome screen
        col1, col2, col3 = st.columns(3)
        with col1:
            st.info("**Step 1**\n\nSelect an education level from the sidebar to begin.")
        with col2:
            st.info("**Step 2**\n\nChoose your state to narrow down results.")
        with col3:
            st.info("**Step 3**\n\nFor K-12 levels, select a county for hyper-local results.")

        st.markdown("---")
        st.markdown("### 📊 Dataset Overview")
        m1, m2, m3, m4 = st.columns(4)
        m1.metric("Total Schools",     len(df))
        m2.metric("States Covered",    df["state"].nunique())
        m3.metric("Education Levels",  df["level"].nunique())
        m4.metric("Avg Rating",        f"{df['rating'].mean():.1f}/10")

    else:
        # ── Filter Summary Banner ──────────────────
        summary = get_filter_summary(
            selected_state, selected_level, selected_county
        )
        st.markdown(
            f'<div class="filter-banner">📍 {summary}</div>',
            unsafe_allow_html=True
        )

        # ── Get filtered schools ───────────────────
        filtered_df = filter_schools(
            df,
            state=selected_state,
            level=selected_level,
            county=selected_county
        )

        # ── Metrics Row ────────────────────────────
        if len(filtered_df) > 0:
            m1, m2, m3, m4 = st.columns(4)
            m1.metric("Schools Found",  len(filtered_df))
            m2.metric("Avg Rating",     f"{filtered_df['rating'].mean():.1f}/10")
            m3.metric("Top Rated",      filtered_df['name'].iloc[
                                            filtered_df['rating'].argmax()
                                        ])
            m4.metric("Public Schools", len(
                filtered_df[filtered_df["type"] == "Public"]
            ))

        st.markdown("---")

        # ── Search or Browse Mode ──────────────────
        if search_clicked and search_query.strip():
            # AI Semantic Search Mode
            st.markdown(f"### 🤖 AI Results for: *\"{search_query}\"*")

            filters = {"state": selected_state, "level": selected_level}
            if selected_county and selected_county != "All Counties":
                filters["county"] = selected_county

            with st.spinner("Searching with AI..."):
                results = query_vector_db(
                    collection,
                    search_query,
                    filters=filters,
                    n_results=n_results
                )

            if results and results["metadatas"][0]:
                for meta, dist in zip(
                    results["metadatas"][0],
                    results["distances"][0]
                ):
                    match_score = round((1 - dist) * 100, 1)
                    school_row  = df[df["name"] == meta["name"]]
                    if not school_row.empty:
                        row = school_row.iloc[0]
                        col_card, col_score = st.columns([4, 1])
                        with col_card:
                            render_school_card(row)
                        with col_score:
                            st.markdown("<br>", unsafe_allow_html=True)
                            st.metric("AI Match", f"{match_score}%")
            else:
                st.markdown(
                    '<div class="no-results">'
                    '🔍 No matching schools found. '
                    'Try different keywords or filters.'
                    '</div>',
                    unsafe_allow_html=True
                )

        else:
            # Browse Mode — show all filtered schools
            if len(filtered_df) > 0:
                st.markdown(
                    f"### 🏫 All {selected_level} schools"
                    f" — {len(filtered_df)} found"
                )
                st.caption(
                    "💡 Tip: Type a search query in the sidebar "
                    "for AI-powered matching"
                )
                # Sort by rating descending
                sorted_df = filtered_df.sort_values(
                    "rating", ascending=False
                ).reset_index(drop=True)
                for _, row in sorted_df.iterrows():
                    render_school_card(row)
            else:
                st.markdown(
                    '<div class="no-results">'
                    '🏫 No schools found for the selected filters.<br>'
                    '<small>Try selecting a different state or county.</small>'
                    '</div>',
                    unsafe_allow_html=True
                )


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
Save the file (Ctrl + S).

            🗓️ Deadline: {row['application_deadline']} &nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;
            🌐 {row['website']}
        </div>
    </div>
    """, unsafe_allow_html=True)
Save (Ctrl + S), then Streamlit will auto-reload. The deadline and website will now render cleanly at the bottom of every card with a subtle divider line.

Why This Happened
The <br><br> tags before the <span> were causing Streamlit's HTML parser to break out of the card block prematurely and treat the remaining content as plain text. Replacing it with a proper <div> with margin fixes this completely.

Check the app in your browser and confirm the cards look clean, then tell me and we move to Phase 4 — Building the Three AI Agents! 🚀still seeing as :<div style="margin-top:0.8rem; padding-top:0.8rem; border-top:1px solid #f0f0f0; font-size:0.8rem; color:#888;">     🗓️ Deadline: July 1 &nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp;     🌐 tamuc.edu </div>Mar 28The issue is that Streamlit is escaping the HTML inside the f-string. Let's fix the entire render_school_card function by simplifying the approach — splitting it into a card with st.container and columns instead of one big HTML block.
Find the entire render_school_card function in app.py and replace it completely with this:
pythondef render_school_card(row):
    rating       = float(row["rating"])
    rating_class = get_rating_class(rating)
    rating_label = get_rating_emoji(rating)

    # Tuition display
    if int(row["tuition_min"]) == 0 and int(row["tuition_max"]) == 0:
        tuition_text = "Free (Public)"
    else:
        tuition_text = f"${int(row['tuition_min']):,} – ${int(row['tuition_max']):,}/yr"

    # Build chips line
    chips = []
    chips.append(f'<span class="chip">💰 {tuition_text}</span>')
    chips.append(f'<span class="chip">👥 {int(row["student_count"]):,} students</span>')
    chips.append(f'<span class="chip">👩‍🏫 Ratio {row["teacher_student_ratio"]}</span>')
    chips.append(f'<span class="chip">🎭 {int(row["clubs"])} clubs</span>')
    if int(row["ap_courses"]) > 0:
        chips.append(f'<span class="chip">📚 {int(row["ap_courses"])} AP Courses</span>')
    chips_html = " ".join(chips)

    # Rating color
    if rating >= 9.0:
        rating_color = "#2e7d32"
        rating_bg    = "#e8f5e9"
    elif rating >= 8.0:
        rating_color = "#f57f17"
        rating_bg    = "#fff8e1"
    else:
        rating_color = "#c62828"
        rating_bg    = "#fce4ec"

    card_html = (
        '<div class="school-card">'
            '<div class="school-name">🏫 ' + str(row["name"]) + '</div>'
            '<div class="school-meta">'
                '📍 ' + str(row["city"]) + ', ' + str(row["county"]) + ' County, ' + str(row["state"]) +
                ' &nbsp;|&nbsp; 🏷️ ' + str(row["type"]) + ' ' + str(row["level"]) +
            '</div>'
            '<div class="school-description">' + str(row["description"]) + '</div>'
            '<span style="display:inline-block; background:' + rating_bg + '; color:' + rating_color + '; '
                'border-radius:20px; padding:2px 12px; font-size:0.85rem; font-weight:600;">'
                + rating_label + ' &nbsp; ' + str(rating) + '/10'
            '</span>'
            '&nbsp;' + chips_html +
            '<div style="margin-top:0.8rem; padding-top:0.8rem; '
                'border-top:1px solid #f0f0f0; font-size:0.8rem; color:#888;">'
                '🗓️ Deadline: ' + str(row["application_deadline"]) +
                ' &nbsp;&nbsp;|&nbsp;&nbsp; 🌐 ' + str(row["website"]) +
            '</div>'
        '</div>'
    )

    st.markdown(card_html, unsafe_allow_html=True)
Save (Ctrl + S) and check the browser.

Why This Fix Works
The previous version used an f-string with triple quotes which caused Streamlit to misinterpret some of the nested HTML tags, especially after line breaks inside the string. Building the HTML using string concatenation instead avoids this problem entirely — Streamlit receives a clean single-line HTML string with no ambiguity.

Agent 1 — The Librarian Agent (RAG)
This agent searches the local ChromaDB vector store and returns structured school summaries using Groq LLM.
Open agents/librarian_agent.py and paste this complete code:
pythonimport os
import logging
import warnings
warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
logging.getLogger("chromadb").setLevel(logging.ERROR)

from groq import Groq
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from utils.embeddings import query_vector_db

load_dotenv()

GROQ_MODEL = os.getenv("GROQ_MODEL", "llama-3.3-70b-versatile")
client     = Groq(api_key=os.getenv("GROQ_API_KEY"))


def librarian_agent(collection, query, filters=None, n_results=5):
    """
    Librarian Agent — searches local ChromaDB vector store
    and uses Groq LLM to generate structured school summaries.

    Returns:
        dict with keys:
            - schools   : list of matched school metadata
            - summary   : LLM-generated comparison summary
            - has_data  : True if local results were found
    """
    print(f"\n📚 Librarian Agent activated for: '{query}'")

    # ── Step 1: Semantic search in ChromaDB ───────
    results = query_vector_db(
        collection,
        query,
        filters=filters,
        n_results=n_results
    )

    schools   = results.get("metadatas", [[]])[0]
    documents = results.get("documents", [[]])[0]
    distances = results.get("distances", [[]])[0]

    if not schools:
        print("   ℹ️ No local results found.")
        return {
            "schools":  [],
            "summary":  "",
            "has_data": False
        }

    print(f"   ✅ Found {len(schools)} schools in local database.")

    # ── Step 2: Build context for LLM ─────────────
    school_context = ""
    for i, (doc, dist) in enumerate(zip(documents, distances)):
        match_score    = round((1 - dist) * 100, 1)
        school_context += f"\n--- School {i+1} (Match: {match_score}%) ---\n"
        school_context += doc + "\n"

    # ── Step 3: Chain-of-Thought prompt ───────────
    cot_prompt = f"""
You are EduNavigator AI, an expert educational consultant.
A user is searching for: "{query}"

Here are the matching schools from our database:
{school_context}

Using Chain-of-Thought reasoning, analyze these schools by:
1. IDENTIFY the most relevant schools for this specific query
2. COMPARE key factors: rating, tuition, programs, class size
3. HIGHLIGHT standout features that match the user's query
4. RECOMMEND the top choice with a clear reason

Provide a concise, helpful summary in this format:

**Top Match:** [School Name]
**Why:** [2-3 sentences explaining why it best matches the query]

**Quick Comparison:**
- [School 1]: [One line highlight]
- [School 2]: [One line highlight]
- [School 3]: [One line highlight]

**Pro Tip:** [One practical advice for the user]

Keep the total response under 200 words. Be specific and helpful.
"""

    # ── Step 4: Get LLM summary ────────────────────
    print("   🤖 Generating AI summary...")
    try:
        response = client.chat.completions.create(
            model=GROQ_MODEL,
            messages=[
                {
                    "role": "system",
                    "content": (
                        "You are EduNavigator AI, a helpful and knowledgeable "
                        "educational consultant. Give concise, accurate, and "
                        "practical advice to students and parents."
                    )
                },
                {
                    "role": "user",
                    "content": cot_prompt
                }
            ],
            max_tokens=400,
            temperature=0.3
        )
        summary = response.choices[0].message.content
        print("   ✅ AI summary generated.")
    except Exception as e:
        summary = f"Summary unavailable: {e}"
        print(f"   ❌ LLM error: {e}")

    return {
        "schools":  schools,
        "summary":  summary,
        "has_data": True
    }
Save (Ctrl + S).

Agent 2 — The Researcher Agent (Web Search)
This agent is triggered when local data is missing or incomplete. It searches the web live using Tavily.
Open agents/researcher_agent.py and paste this:
pythonimport os
import logging
import warnings
warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
logging.getLogger("chromadb").setLevel(logging.ERROR)

from groq import Groq
from tavily import TavilyClient
from dotenv import load_dotenv

load_dotenv()

GROQ_MODEL  = os.getenv("GROQ_MODEL", "llama-3.3-70b-versatile")
groq_client = Groq(api_key=os.getenv("GROQ_API_KEY"))
tavily      = TavilyClient(api_key=os.getenv("TAVILY_API_KEY"))


def researcher_agent(query, state=None, level=None, n_results=5):
    """
    Researcher Agent — searches the web live using Tavily
    when local ChromaDB data is missing or insufficient.

    Returns:
        dict with keys:
            - web_results : raw Tavily search results
            - summary     : LLM-generated summary from web data
            - sources     : list of source URLs found
    """
    print(f"\n🔍 Researcher Agent activated for: '{query}'")

    # ── Step 1: Build targeted search query ───────
    location_context = ""
    if state:
        location_context += f" in {state}"
    if level:
        location_context += f" {level}"

    search_query = f"{query}{location_context} ratings fees admission requirements 2024"
    print(f"   🌐 Searching web for: '{search_query}'")

    # ── Step 2: Tavily web search ──────────────────
    try:
        search_results = tavily.search(
            query      = search_query,
            max_results= n_results,
            search_depth="advanced"
        )
        web_results = search_results.get("results", [])
        print(f"   ✅ Found {len(web_results)} web results.")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"   ❌ Tavily error: {e}")
        return {
            "web_results": [],
            "summary":     f"Web search failed: {e}",
            "sources":     []
        }

    if not web_results:
        return {
            "web_results": [],
            "summary":     "No web results found.",
            "sources":     []
        }

    # ── Step 3: Build context from web results ────
    web_context = ""
    sources     = []
    for i, result in enumerate(web_results):
        web_context += f"\n--- Source {i+1} ---\n"
        web_context += f"Title  : {result.get('title', 'N/A')}\n"
        web_context += f"URL    : {result.get('url', 'N/A')}\n"
        web_context += f"Content: {result.get('content', 'N/A')[:500]}\n"
        sources.append({
            "title": result.get("title", "N/A"),
            "url":   result.get("url",   "N/A")
        })

    # ── Step 4: Chain-of-Thought LLM synthesis ────
    cot_prompt = f"""
You are EduNavigator AI, an expert educational researcher.
A user is looking for: "{query}"
Location context: {location_context if location_context else "Not specified"}

I searched the web and found these results:
{web_context}

Using Chain-of-Thought reasoning:
1. EXTRACT key facts about schools mentioned (name, location, ratings, fees)
2. IDENTIFY the most relevant institutions for this query
3. SYNTHESIZE the information into actionable insights
4. HIGHLIGHT any scholarships, deadlines, or special programs mentioned

Provide your response in this format:

**Schools Found Online:**
- [School Name] | [Location] | [Key fact about rating or fee]
- [School Name] | [Location] | [Key fact about rating or fee]

**Key Insights:**
[2-3 sentences summarizing the most important findings]

**Important Deadlines/Requirements:**
[Any deadlines or requirements found in the search results]

**Recommended Next Steps:**
[2 practical steps the user should take]

Keep response under 250 words. Be specific and factual.
"""

    print("   🤖 Synthesizing web results with AI...")
    try:
        response = groq_client.chat.completions.create(
            model=GROQ_MODEL,
            messages=[
                {
                    "role": "system",
                    "content": (
                        "You are EduNavigator AI, a thorough educational "
                        "researcher. Extract and synthesize accurate "
                        "information from web sources to help students "
                        "and parents make informed decisions."
                    )
                },
                {
                    "role": "user",
                    "content": cot_prompt
                }
            ],
            max_tokens=500,
            temperature=0.2
        )
        summary = response.choices[0].message.content
        print("   ✅ Web research summary generated.")
    except Exception as e:
        summary = f"Summary unavailable: {e}"
        print(f"   ❌ LLM error: {e}")

    return {
        "web_results": web_results,
        "summary":     summary,
        "sources":     sources
    }
Save (Ctrl + S).

Agent 3 — The Document Specialist Agent (PDF Checklist)
This agent analyzes admission requirements and generates a personalized PDF checklist.
Open agents/doc_specialist_agent.py and paste this:
pythonimport os
import logging
import warnings
warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
logging.getLogger("chromadb").setLevel(logging.ERROR)

from groq import Groq
from fpdf import FPDF
from dotenv import load_dotenv
from datetime import datetime

load_dotenv()

GROQ_MODEL   = os.getenv("GROQ_MODEL",   "llama-3.3-70b-versatile")
OUTPUT_PATH  = os.getenv("OUTPUT_PATH",  "./outputs")
groq_client  = Groq(api_key=os.getenv("GROQ_API_KEY"))

os.makedirs(OUTPUT_PATH, exist_ok=True)


def _generate_checklist_items(school_name, level, state, extra_context=""):
    """
    Use Groq LLM with CoT prompting to generate a
    personalized application checklist for a school.
    """
    cot_prompt = f"""
You are EduNavigator AI, an expert college and school admissions consultant.

Generate a detailed application checklist for:
School : {school_name}
Level  : {level}
State  : {state}
Context: {extra_context if extra_context else "Standard application"}

Using Chain-of-Thought reasoning:
1. CONSIDER the education level and typical requirements
2. IDENTIFY standard documents needed for this level
3. ADD level-specific requirements (SAT for universities, immunizations for preschool etc.)
4. INCLUDE timeline and deadlines advice
5. ADD scholarship and financial aid items if applicable

Return ONLY a JSON object in exactly this format, no other text:
{{
  "checklist": {{
    "Academic Documents": [
      "Item 1",
      "Item 2"
    ],
    "Personal Documents": [
      "Item 1",
      "Item 2"
    ],
    "Application Requirements": [
      "Item 1",
      "Item 2"
    ],
    "Financial Documents": [
      "Item 1",
      "Item 2"
    ],
    "Important Deadlines": [
      "Item 1",
      "Item 2"
    ]
  }},
  "tips": [
    "Tip 1",
    "Tip 2",
    "Tip 3"
  ]
}}
"""
    response = groq_client.chat.completions.create(
        model=GROQ_MODEL,
        messages=[
            {
                "role": "system",
                "content": (
                    "You are an admissions expert. "
                    "Return only valid JSON, no markdown, "
                    "no explanation, no code blocks."
                )
            },
            {
                "role": "user",
                "content": cot_prompt
            }
        ],
        max_tokens=800,
        temperature=0.1
    )
    return response.choices[0].message.content


def _build_pdf(school_name, level, state, checklist_data, tips):
    """Build and save the PDF checklist file."""

    class EduPDF(FPDF):
        def header(self):
            self.set_fill_color(30, 58, 95)
            self.rect(0, 0, 210, 28, "F")
            self.set_font("Helvetica", "B", 16)
            self.set_text_color(255, 255, 255)
            self.set_xy(0, 8)
            self.cell(0, 12, "EduNavigator AI — Application Checklist", align="C")
            self.set_text_color(0, 0, 0)
            self.ln(24)

        def footer(self):
            self.set_y(-15)
            self.set_font("Helvetica", "I", 8)
            self.set_text_color(150, 150, 150)
            self.cell(
                0, 10,
                f"Generated by EduNavigator AI  |  "
                f"{datetime.now().strftime('%B %d, %Y')}  |  "
                f"Page {self.page_no()}",
                align="C"
            )

    pdf = EduPDF()
    pdf.add_page()
    pdf.set_auto_page_break(auto=True, margin=20)

    # ── School Info Block ──────────────────────────
    pdf.set_fill_color(227, 242, 253)
    pdf.rect(10, 30, 190, 22, "F")
    pdf.set_font("Helvetica", "B", 13)
    pdf.set_text_color(30, 58, 95)
    pdf.set_xy(14, 33)
    pdf.cell(0, 7, f"School: {school_name}", ln=True)
    pdf.set_font("Helvetica", "", 10)
    pdf.set_text_color(80, 80, 80)
    pdf.set_x(14)
    pdf.cell(
        0, 6,
        f"Level: {level}   |   State: {state}   |   "
        f"Generated: {datetime.now().strftime('%B %d, %Y')}",
        ln=True
    )
    pdf.ln(10)

    # ── Checklist Sections ─────────────────────────
    section_colors = {
        "Academic Documents":       (232, 245, 233),
        "Personal Documents":       (243, 229, 245),
        "Application Requirements": (227, 242, 253),
        "Financial Documents":      (255, 248, 225),
        "Important Deadlines":      (252, 228, 236),
    }

    for section, items in checklist_data.items():
        if not items:
            continue

        # Section header
        r, g, b = section_colors.get(section, (240, 240, 240))
        pdf.set_fill_color(r, g, b)
        pdf.set_font("Helvetica", "B", 11)
        pdf.set_text_color(30, 58, 95)
        pdf.set_x(10)
        pdf.cell(190, 8, f"  {section}", fill=True, ln=True)
        pdf.ln(2)

        # Checklist items with checkboxes
        pdf.set_font("Helvetica", "", 10)
        pdf.set_text_color(50, 50, 50)
        for item in items:
            pdf.set_x(14)
            pdf.cell(8,  7, "[ ]")
            pdf.cell(172, 7, item, ln=True)
        pdf.ln(4)

    # ── Tips Section ───────────────────────────────
    if tips:
        pdf.set_fill_color(30, 58, 95)
        pdf.set_font("Helvetica", "B", 11)
        pdf.set_text_color(255, 255, 255)
        pdf.set_x(10)
        pdf.cell(190, 8, "  Pro Tips from EduNavigator AI", fill=True, ln=True)
        pdf.ln(2)

        pdf.set_font("Helvetica", "", 10)
        pdf.set_text_color(50, 50, 50)
        for i, tip in enumerate(tips, 1):
            pdf.set_x(14)
            pdf.multi_cell(182, 6, f"{i}. {tip}")
            pdf.ln(1)

    # ── Save PDF ───────────────────────────────────
    safe_name = school_name.replace(" ", "_").replace("/", "-")
    filename  = f"{safe_name}_checklist.pdf"
    filepath  = os.path.join(OUTPUT_PATH, filename)
    pdf.output(filepath)
    return filepath


def doc_specialist_agent(school_name, level, state, extra_context=""):
    """
    Document Specialist Agent — generates a personalized
    PDF application checklist for a given school.

    Returns:
        dict with keys:
            - filepath     : path to the generated PDF
            - checklist    : dict of checklist sections
            - tips         : list of pro tips
            - school_name  : name of the school
    """
    print(f"\n📄 Doc Specialist Agent activated for: '{school_name}'")

    # ── Step 1: Generate checklist via LLM ────────
    print("   🤖 Generating personalized checklist...")
    try:
        raw_response = _generate_checklist_items(
            school_name, level, state, extra_context
        )

        # Clean response and parse JSON
        import json
        clean = raw_response.strip()
        if clean.startswith("```"):
            clean = clean.split("```")[1]
            if clean.startswith("json"):
                clean = clean[4:]
        clean = clean.strip()

        parsed      = json.loads(clean)
        checklist   = parsed.get("checklist", {})
        tips        = parsed.get("tips", [])
        print(f"   ✅ Checklist generated with {sum(len(v) for v in checklist.values())} items.")

    except Exception as e:
        print(f"   ❌ LLM/parse error: {e}")
        # Fallback checklist
        checklist = {
            "Academic Documents":       ["Official transcripts", "Test scores (SAT/ACT if applicable)"],
            "Personal Documents":       ["Government-issued ID", "Proof of residency"],
            "Application Requirements": ["Completed application form", "Personal statement or essay"],
            "Financial Documents":      ["Financial aid forms (FAFSA if applicable)", "Proof of income"],
            "Important Deadlines":      ["Check school website for current deadlines"]
        }
        tips = [
            "Start your application at least 3 months before the deadline.",
            "Keep copies of all submitted documents.",
            "Follow up with the admissions office after submission."
        ]

    # ── Step 2: Build PDF ──────────────────────────
    print("   📝 Building PDF checklist...")
    try:
        filepath = _build_pdf(school_name, level, state, checklist, tips)
        print(f"   ✅ PDF saved to: {filepath}")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"   ❌ PDF error: {e}")
        filepath = None

    return {
        "filepath":    filepath,
        "checklist":   checklist,
        "tips":        tips,
        "school_name": school_name
    }
Save (Ctrl + S).

Issue 1 — Wrong Model Name
The .env file has groq_model=llama-3.3-70b-versatile instead of just llama-3.3-70b-versatile. The variable name got included in the value.
Open .env and check your GROQ_MODEL line. It likely looks like this:
envGROQ_MODEL=groq_model=llama-3.3-70b-versatile
Fix it to:
envGROQ_MODEL=llama-3.3-70b-versatile
Save (Ctrl + S).

Issue 2 — PDF Font Doesn't Support Special Characters
The — dash character in "EduNavigator AI — Application Checklist" is not supported by the built-in Helvetica font in fpdf2. Fix it by replacing the special character with a plain hyphen.
Open agents/doc_specialist_agent.py and find this line inside the header method:
pythonself.cell(0, 12, "EduNavigator AI — Application Checklist", align="C")
Replace it with:
pythonself.cell(0, 12, "EduNavigator AI - Application Checklist", align="C")
Also find the footer method and fix this line:
pythonf"Generated by EduNavigator AI  |  "
The footer is fine — but while you're there, also check the tips section in _build_pdf for this line:
pythonpdf.cell(190, 8, "  Pro Tips from EduNavigator AI", fill=True, ln=True)
That's fine too. Only the — character needs fixing.
Save (Ctrl + S).

Phase 5 Preview — The Orchestrator
Phase 5 — Agent Orchestrator
│
├── Receives user query + filters from UI
├── Calls Librarian Agent first (local RAG)
├── If results insufficient → calls Researcher Agent (web)
├── Combines both results into one unified response
└── Offers PDF checklist generation for any school found
The Orchestrator is the brain that decides which agents to call and when. After Phase 5 the entire system will be wired together end to end.
Type "ready" and we build Phase 5! 🚀readyMar 28Phase 5 — The Agent Orchestrator
The Orchestrator is the master controller that decides which agents to call, when to call them, and how to combine their results into one unified response.

Step 1 — Build the Orchestrator
Open agents/orchestrator.py and paste this complete code:
pythonimport os
import logging
import warnings
warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")
logging.getLogger("chromadb").setLevel(logging.ERROR)

from dotenv import load_dotenv
from agents.librarian_agent      import librarian_agent
from agents.researcher_agent     import researcher_agent
from agents.doc_specialist_agent import doc_specialist_agent

load_dotenv()

# Minimum number of local results before
# triggering the Researcher Agent
MIN_LOCAL_RESULTS = 2


def orchestrator(
    collection,
    query,
    state        = None,
    level        = None,
    county       = None,
    n_results    = 5,
    generate_pdf = False,
    school_name  = None
):
    """
    Master Orchestrator — coordinates all three agents.

    Decision Logic:
        1. Always call Librarian Agent first (local RAG)
        2. If local results < MIN_LOCAL_RESULTS,
           call Researcher Agent (live web search)
        3. If generate_pdf=True,
           call Doc Specialist Agent (PDF checklist)
        4. Combine and return unified response

    Returns:
        dict with keys:
            - source          : 'local', 'web', or 'both'
            - schools         : list of school metadata (local)
            - local_summary   : LLM summary from Librarian
            - web_summary     : LLM summary from Researcher
            - web_sources     : list of web source URLs
            - pdf_result      : PDF generation result or None
            - query           : original query
            - filters_used    : filters applied
            - agents_called   : list of agents that were called
    """

    print("\n" + "=" * 55)
    print("🎯 ORCHESTRATOR ACTIVATED")
    print(f"   Query  : {query}")
    print(f"   State  : {state}")
    print(f"   Level  : {level}")
    print(f"   County : {county}")
    print("=" * 55)

    response = {
        "source":        None,
        "schools":       [],
        "local_summary": "",
        "web_summary":   "",
        "web_sources":   [],
        "pdf_result":    None,
        "query":         query,
        "filters_used":  {
            "state":  state,
            "level":  level,
            "county": county
        },
        "agents_called": []
    }

    # ── Build filters for vector DB query ─────────
    filters = {}
    if state:
        filters["state"] = state
    if level:
        filters["level"] = level
    if county and county not in ["All Counties", "Select County"]:
        filters["county"] = county

    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    # STEP 1 — Librarian Agent (always runs first)
    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    print("\n📋 Step 1: Calling Librarian Agent...")
    librarian_result = librarian_agent(
        collection = collection,
        query      = query,
        filters    = filters,
        n_results  = n_results
    )
    response["agents_called"].append("Librarian")
    response["schools"]       = librarian_result["schools"]
    response["local_summary"] = librarian_result["summary"]

    local_count = len(librarian_result["schools"])
    print(f"   📊 Local results: {local_count}")

    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    # STEP 2 — Researcher Agent
    # Triggered when local results are insufficient
    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    needs_web_search = (
        not librarian_result["has_data"] or
        local_count < MIN_LOCAL_RESULTS
    )

    # Also trigger web search if query contains
    # a specific school name not in local DB
    specific_school_keywords = [
        "ut austin", "university of texas austin",
        "harvard", "stanford", "mit", "yale",
        "texas tech", "baylor", "rice university",
        "tcu", "texas christian"
    ]
    query_lower = query.lower()
    is_specific_school = any(
        kw in query_lower for kw in specific_school_keywords
    )

    if needs_web_search or is_specific_school:
        reason = (
            "specific school detected"
            if is_specific_school
            else f"only {local_count} local results found"
        )
        print(f"\n📋 Step 2: Calling Researcher Agent ({reason})...")
        researcher_result = researcher_agent(
            query     = query,
            state     = state,
            level     = level,
            n_results = n_results
        )
        response["agents_called"].append("Researcher")
        response["web_summary"] = researcher_result["summary"]
        response["web_sources"] = researcher_result["sources"]

        # Set source flag
        if local_count > 0:
            response["source"] = "both"
        else:
            response["source"] = "web"
    else:
        print(f"\n   ✅ Sufficient local results ({local_count}). Skipping web search.")
        response["source"] = "local"

    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    # STEP 3 — Doc Specialist Agent (optional)
    # Only runs when generate_pdf=True
    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    if generate_pdf and school_name:
        print(f"\n📋 Step 3: Calling Doc Specialist Agent for '{school_name}'...")
        pdf_result = doc_specialist_agent(
            school_name   = school_name,
            level         = level or "University",
            state         = state or "Texas",
            extra_context = query
        )
        response["agents_called"].append("DocSpecialist")
        response["pdf_result"] = pdf_result
    else:
        print("\n   ℹ️ PDF generation not requested. Skipping Doc Specialist.")

    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    # FINAL SUMMARY
    # ══════════════════════════════════════════════
    print("\n" + "=" * 55)
    print("✅ ORCHESTRATOR COMPLETE")
    print(f"   Agents called : {', '.join(response['agents_called'])}")
    print(f"   Source        : {response['source']}")
    print(f"   Local schools : {len(response['schools'])}")
    print(f"   Web sources   : {len(response['web_sources'])}")
    print(f"   PDF generated : {response['pdf_result'] is not None}")
    print("=" * 55)

    return response
Save (Ctrl + S).

pythonimport warnings
import logging

result1 = orchestrator(
    collection = collection,
    query      = "best high school with AP courses",

)

print("-" * 55)
result3 = orchestrator(
    collection   = collection,
    query        = "Plano Senior High admission requirements",
    state        = "Texas",
    level        = "High School",
    n_results    = 3,
    generate_pdf = True,
    school_name  = "Plano Senior High"
)
print(f"\n✅ Source        : {result3['source']}")
print(f"✅ Agents called : {result3['agents_called']}")
if result3["pdf_result"]:
    print(f"✅ PDF saved to  : {result3['pdf_result']['filepath']}")
    print(f"✅ Total items   : {sum(len(v) for v in result3['pdf_result']['checklist'].values())}")

# ══════════════════════════════════════════════════
# TEST 4 — No filters (broad search)
# ══════════════════════════════════════════════════
print("\n\nTEST 4 — Broad search across all Texas universities")
print("-" * 55)
result4 = orchestrator(
    collection = collection,
    query      = "affordable university with scholarships and engineering",
    state      = "Texas",
    level      = "University",
    n_results  = 5
)
print(f"\n✅ Source        : {result4['source']}")
print(f"✅ Agents called : {result4['agents_called']}")
print(f"✅ Schools found : {len(result4['schools'])}")
print(f"\nLocal Summary:\n{result4['local_summary']}")

print("\n" + "=" * 55)
print("✅ Phase 5 Complete! Orchestrator working.")
print("=" * 55)
